    .<!--% NOTE I feel obligated to contend that the foliation 38 on folio from ms. L 631 is most probably inaccurate. This is shown by the fact that there is a fragment of ms. L 631 which is parallel to folio 31-32 in ms. L 298. Within this ms., the words gaṇitha, kalaṣaya, kagaṣa, ḍaṇḍala, canḍa, R̥kta, kraṣa, kalmaṣa, preta and so on are the synonyms of pā, not asu as it seems to be pointed out at ms. L 631. If we look at folios 30-32 of ms. L 298, we can see that there are at least 22 more sorts of synonyms following the synonym of the word pa, with at least 170 words in total until we reach the synonym of the word asu. So after the number 37 of ms. L 631, at least we miss two folios as this amount of words that can fit on each page. However, ms. L 631’s fragment demonstrates that one of the two missing folios survives, although with left and right sides damage. Then my three conclusions are as follows: (1) the fact that the jumping content from foliation 37 to 38 does not indicate that the original source was corrupted in any way; rather, it was simply a foliation error committed either after the copy was created; (2) the damage to the right and left sides of the following folio occurred long before this manuscript was brought to the National Library of Republic Indonesia in 1856 or 1857; and (3) the numbering that was done, both written in ’Old style’ Javanese or Latin letters, was done after the damage had occurred.%-->
    .
